data-file-width="640" data-file-height="362" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Steel_Distribution_Depot_-_geograph.org.uk_-_236054.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wednesfield Steelpark in September 2006</div></div></div>\n<p>On the Staffordshire boundary, to the west on the Pendeford Business Park, are <a href="/wiki/ADAS_(company)" title="ADAS (company)">ADAS</a> (previously on the A41 in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wergs&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wergs (page does not exist)">Wergs</a>), <a href="/wiki/Gunnebo_Security_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Gunnebo Security Group">Gunnebo</a> UK (<a href="/wiki/Automated_cash_handling" title="Automated cash handling">cash handling</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Midshires" title="Birmingham Midshires">Birmingham Midshires</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turner_Powertrain_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Turner Powertrain Systems (page does not exist)">Turner Powertrain Systems</a> is the world market leader for transmissions for <a href="/wiki/Backhoe_loader" title="Backhoe loader">backhoe loaders</a>, mini <a href="/wiki/Excavator" title="Excavator">excavators</a> <a href="/wiki/Telescopic_handler" title="Telescopic handler">telescopic handlers</a>, and site dumpers is further south, to the west of the A449 near <a href="/wiki/Dunstall_Hill" title="Dunstall Hill">Dunstall Hill</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hampson_Industries" title="Hampson Industries">Hampson Industries</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Brierley_Hill" title="Brierley Hill">Brierley Hill</a>. Wednesbury Tube (part of <a href="/wiki/Mueller_Industries" title="Mueller Industries">Mueller Industries</a>) make <a href="/wiki/Copper_tubing" title="Copper tubing">copper pipe</a> on the A41 in Bilston at the Key Ind Est near the <a href="/wiki/Loxdale_tram_stop" title="Loxdale tram stop">Loxdale tram stop</a>, and its sister company <a href="/w/index.php?title=Primaflow&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Primaflow (page does not exist)">Primaflow</a> makes brass fittings in Nechells. On the A4124, Tata Steel (former site of British Steel Seamless Tubes until 1995) have their <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wednesfield_Steelpark&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wednesfield Steelpark (page does not exist)">Wednesfield Steelpark</a> (the UK\'s biggest steelyard, built by Corus in 1999) on the Walsall boundary. \n</p><p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boss_Design&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Boss Design (page does not exist)">Boss Design</a> is a furniture manufacturer in Blowers Green, Dudley at the <a href="/wiki/A461_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A461 road">A461</a>/A459 roundabout. <a href="/wiki/KUKA" title="KUKA">KUKA</a> Robotics UK, a maker of industrial robots, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Joseph_Ash&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Joseph Ash (page does not exist)">Joseph Ash</a> (galvinizers) are off the A459 at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mucklow_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mucklow Hill (page does not exist)">Mucklow Hill</a> in Halesowen, with <a href="/wiki/Floors-2-Go" title="Floors-2-Go">Floors-2-Go</a> based off the <a href="/wiki/A458_road" title="A458 road">A458</a>; <a href="/wiki/Sandvik" title="Sandvik">Sandvik</a> Coromant UK (Swedish machine cutting tools, who provide Birmingham\'s <a href="/wiki/Christmas_tree" title="Christmas tree">Christmas tree</a>) are off junction 3 of the M5 on the A456. Hingley Trailers (former M+G Trailers before 2009) makes <a href="/wiki/Semi-trailer" title="Semi-trailer">trailers</a> on the <a href="/wiki/A458_road" title="A458 road">A458</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lye,_West_Midlands" title="Lye, West Midlands">Lye</a>. <a href="/wiki/Marcegaglia" title="Marcegaglia">Marcegaglia</a> UK make electrical-resistance welded steel tubes off the <a href="/wiki/A461_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A461 road">A461</a> in Dudley. <a href="/wiki/Essar_Group" title="Essar Group">Essar Steel</a> UK (former <a href="/w/index.php?title=Servosteel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Servosteel (page does not exist)">Servosteel</a>) on the A4101 Pensnett Road in west Dudley, is the largest independent steel toll processor in the UK. <a href="/wiki/Rentokil_Initial" title="Rentokil Initial">Initial Cleaning Services</a> (Facilities) is based on the Ashmore Ind Estate, at the <a href="/wiki/A461_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A461 road">A461</a>/A459 Castle Gate Island roundabout, opposite the <a href="/wiki/Showcase_Cinemas" title="Showcase Cinemas">Showcase</a> cinema on the Castle Gate Leisure Park. The <a href="/wiki/Merry_Hill_Shopping_Centre" title="Merry Hill Shopping Centre">Merry Hill Shopping Centre</a>, similar to <a href="/wiki/Meadowhall_(shopping_centre)" title="Meadowhall (shopping centre)">Meadowhall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a>, is built on a large former steelworks, the <a href="/wiki/Round_Oak_Steelworks" title="Round Oak Steelworks">Round Oak Steelworks</a>. \n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Avery_Weigh-Tronix" title="Avery Weigh-Tronix">Avery Weigh-Tronix</a> is on the site of James Watt\'s <a href="/wiki/Soho_Foundry" title="Soho Foundry">Soho Foundry</a> in <a href="/wiki/Smethwick" title="Smethwick">Smethwick</a>; <a href="/w/index.php?title=Interlink_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Interlink Express (page does not exist)">Interlink Express</a> (and its parent <a href="/w/index.php?title=GeoPost&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="GeoPost (page does not exist)">GeoPost</a> UK) is on Summit Crescent Ind Estate off the <a href="/wiki/A4252_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A4252 road">A4252</a>, north of <a href="/wiki/Smethwick_Galton_Bridge_railway_station" title="Smethwick Galton Bridge railway station">Smethwick Galton Bridge railway station</a>, next to the M5. <a href="/wiki/Hadley_Group" title="Hadley Group">Hadley Group</a> near the Soho Foundry is the largest <a href="/wiki/Rolling_(metalworking)" title="Rolling (metalworking)">cold roll forming</a> manufacturer in the UK. J. B. &amp; S. Lees makes <a href="/wiki/Strip_steel" title="Strip steel">steel strip</a> at the Trident Steel Works in Albion, West Bromwich off the B4166 and also by <a href="/wiki/Firth_Cleveland" class="mw-redirect" title="Firth Cleveland">Firth Cleveland</a> at the B4517/B4163 junction in Tipton further up the Birmingham Canal. Caparo Precision Tubes between the M5 and A4182 in Oldbury, is the UK\'s largest producer of <a href="/wiki/Electric_resistance_welding" title="Electric resistance welding">electric resistance welded</a> (ERW) steel tubes, and <a href="/wiki/Wellman_Group" title="Wellman Group">Wellman Group</a> make boilers off the A457 to the west. <a href="/wiki/Metsec" title="Metsec">Metsec</a>, east of Oldbury (owned by <a href="/wiki/Voestalpine" title="Voestalpine">Voestalpine</a>), is one of the UK\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Rolling_(metalworking)" title="Rolling (metalworking)">cold roll-forming</a> companies. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Conex_B%C3%A4nninger&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Conex B\xc3\xa4nninger (page does not exist)">Conex B\xc3\xa4nninger</a> (former IBP Conex), on the B4166 in New Town, west of West Bromwich on Birmingham Canal, make <a href="/wiki/Pipe_fitting" title="Pipe fitting">pipe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Compression_fitting" title="Compression fitting">compression fittings</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rhodia_(company)" title="Rhodia (company)">Rhodia</a>\'s Oldbury site on the B4170 in <a href="/wiki/Langley_Green,_West_Midlands" title="Langley Green, West Midlands">Langley Green</a>, south of Oldbury and east of the M5 is a world-leading site (former <a href="/wiki/Albright_and_Wilson" title="Albright and Wilson">Albright and Wilson</a>) in phosphorus-based chemistry. The AA have a main office on the A4123 at the A4034 roundabout in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rounds_Green&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rounds Green (page does not exist)">Rounds Green</a>, west of Oldbury. <a href="/w/index.php?title=BIP_Chemicals&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="BIP Chemicals (page does not exist)">BIP Chemicals</a> (former British Cyanides) at Oldbury are the oldest polymer manufacturer in the UK. STILL UK (<a href="/wiki/KION_Group" title="KION Group">KION Group</a>) is in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Harvills_Hawthorn&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Harvills Hawthorn (page does not exist)">Harvills Hawthorn</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Golds_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Golds Hill (page does not exist)">Golds Hill</a> at the A461/A41 roundabout, north-west of West Bromwich; further along the A41 is <a href="/wiki/2_Sisters_Food_Group" title="2 Sisters Food Group">2 Sisters Food Group</a>, Britain\'s largest processor of chicken. Nesbit Evans in the east of Wednesbury, off the A41, are a main manufacturer of hospital beds, owned by <a href="/wiki/ArjoHuntleigh" title="ArjoHuntleigh">ArjoHuntleigh</a>. \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chubb_building.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Chubb_building.jpg/220px-Chubb_building.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Chubb_building.jpg/330px-Chubb_building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Chubb_building.jpg/440px-Chubb_building.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="355" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chubb_building.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Willenhall is the lockmaking capital of the UK, and the home of Chubb</div></div></div>\n<p>The national headquarters of <a href="/wiki/One_Stop" class="mw-redirect" title="One Stop">One Stop</a> is on the A4124 in <a href="/wiki/Brownhills" title="Brownhills">Brownhills</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Clayhanger,_West_Midlands" title="Clayhanger, West Midlands">Clayhanger</a>. <a href="/wiki/Homeserve" title="Homeserve">Homeserve</a> is in the north of Walsall on the <a href="/wiki/A34_road" title="A34 road">A34</a>, opposite Walsall Retail Park; next door to the north, on the other side of the <a href="/wiki/Wyrley_and_Essington_Canal" title="Wyrley and Essington Canal">Wyrley and Essington Canal</a> on the B4210, on the edge of <a href="/wiki/Blakenall_Heath" title="Blakenall Heath">Blakenall Heath</a>, is <a href="/w/index.php?title=Eagle_Envelopes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eagle Envelopes (page does not exist)">Eagle Envelopes</a>, part of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayer-Kuvert&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mayer-Kuvert (page does not exist)">Mayer-Kuvert</a>, Europe\'s leading envelope manufacturer. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Imperial_Bathroom_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Imperial Bathroom Company (page does not exist)">Imperial Bathroom Company</a>, on the Empire Ind Est off the B4152 in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Leighswood&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Leighswood (page does not exist)">Leighswood</a>, is in the north of Walsall borough; next door is <a href="/wiki/RMD_Kwikform" title="RMD Kwikform">RMD Kwikform</a> (scaffolding) on the opposite side of <a href="/wiki/Rushall_Canal" title="Rushall Canal">Rushall Canal</a>; to the south was GKN Driveline Walsall from 1953 until 2010, which was the largest independent manufacturer of <a href="/wiki/Constant-velocity_joint" title="Constant-velocity joint">CV-jointed</a> <a href="/wiki/Drive_shaft" title="Drive shaft">propshafts</a> in Europe. <a href="/wiki/Poundland" title="Poundland">Poundland</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Willenhall" title="Willenhall">Willenhall</a>, on the side of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Country_Route" title="Black Country Route">Black Country Route</a> (<a href="/wiki/A454_road" title="A454 road">A454</a>) towards the M6 junction 11. <a href="/wiki/Wedge_Group" title="Wedge Group">Wedge Group</a>, based on the B4484 in Willenhall, is the largest <a href="/wiki/Hot-dip_galvanizing" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot-dip galvanizing">hot dip galvanising</a> company in the UK. <a href="/wiki/Assa_Abloy" title="Assa Abloy">Assa Abloy</a> UK (and <a href="/wiki/Yale_(company)" title="Yale (company)">Yale</a> UK, former Yale &amp; Towne), owned by a Swedish company, is off the A454 at the B4464 roundabout in Willenhall, as the town is known for manufacture of locks; close by is <a href="/wiki/A.F._Blakemore" class="mw-redirect" title="A.F. Blakemore">A.F. Blakemore</a>, which supplies most of the <a href="/wiki/Spar_(retailer)" title="Spar (retailer)">SPAR</a> shops in the UK. <a href="/wiki/ZF_Friedrichshafen" title="ZF Friedrichshafen">ZF Lemf\xc3\xb6rder UK</a> make chassis components (a main competitor to GKN), in the east of Darlaston, with <a href="/wiki/Caparo" title="Caparo">Caparo</a> Atlas Fastenings off the A4038.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Worcestershire">Worcestershire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Midlands_(region)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Worcestershire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing_in_Worcester" class="mw-redirect" title="Manufacturing in Worcester">Manufacturing in Worcester</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Worcester_Bosch_-_geograph.org.uk_-_57948.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Worcester_Bosch_-_geograph.org.uk_-_57948.jpg/220px-Worcester_Bosch_-_geograph.org.uk_-_57948.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Worcester_Bosch_-_geograph.org.uk_-_57948.jpg/330px-Worcester_Bosch_-_geograph.org.uk_-_57948.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Worcester_Bosch_-_geograph.org.uk_-_57948.jpg/440px-Worcester_Bosch_-_geograph.org.uk_-_57948.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Worcester_Bosch_-_geograph.org.uk_-_57948.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Worcester Bosch; Bosch Thermotechnology are in <a href="/wiki/Warndon" title="Warndon">Warndon</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In Redditch are <a href="/wiki/Halfords" title="Halfords">Halfords</a>, on the B4497 to the south in <a href="/wiki/Washford,_Worcestershire" class="mw-redirect" title="Washford, Worcestershire">Washford</a>, and <a href="/wiki/GKN" title="GKN">GKN</a> (it has the second largest turnover in the West Midlands) is on the <a href="/wiki/A441_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A441 road">A441</a> in <a href="/wiki/Riverside,_Worcestershire" class="mw-redirect" title="Riverside, Worcestershire">Riverside</a>. CompAir Hydrovane, who make <a href="/wiki/Rotary_vane_pump" title="Rotary vane pump">rotary vane</a> compressors, are on the <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Redditch" title="Districts of Redditch">Washford</a> Ind Estate near the B4497/A453 junction in Redditch. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mettis_Aerospace&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mettis Aerospace (page does not exist)">Mettis Aerospace</a> are on the B4184 in Enfield, north Redditch, and make light metal components (the former <a href="/wiki/High_Duty_Alloys_Ltd." class="mw-redirect" title="High Duty Alloys Ltd.">High Duty Alloys</a>, which made most of the <a href="/wiki/Forging" title="Forging">forged</a> pistons for Britain\'s aircraft engines in WWII). <a href="/wiki/Hymatic" title="Hymatic">Hymatic</a> (part of Honeywell Defense and Space) make world-leading <a href="/wiki/Cryocooler" title="Cryocooler">cryocoolers</a>, on Moon\'s Moat Ind Est, in the north-east of Redditch; on same site the <a href="/w/index.php?title=KAC_Alarm_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="KAC Alarm Company (page does not exist)">KAC Alarm Company</a>, also part of Honeywell, make <a href="/wiki/Manual_fire_alarm_activation" title="Manual fire alarm activation">break glass call points</a> for <a href="/wiki/Fire_alarm_system" title="Fire alarm system">fire alarms</a>; they innovated them in the 1970s, and are global leaders. <a href="/wiki/Magna_International" title="Magna International">Magna Interior Systems</a> make the cockpit module (<a href="/wiki/Dashboard" title="Dashboard">dashboard</a>) for the MINI. <a href="/wiki/Henry_Milward_%26_Sons" title="Henry Milward &amp; Sons">Entaco</a> make needles for hand sewing and medical purposes in the south of Redditch on the Washford Ind Est. Directly east of Redditch in <a href="/wiki/Beoley" title="Beoley">Beoley</a> is <a href="/wiki/Lear_Corporation" title="Lear Corporation">Lear Corporation</a> UK, who make car seats. <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Group_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenix Group (company)">Phoenix Group</a> (non-public <a href="/wiki/Life_insurance" title="Life insurance">life assurance</a> schemes) is off the A435 in the north-east of the county near the Warwickshire boundary, at <a href="/wiki/Wythall" title="Wythall">Wythall</a>, and has a large turnover; nearby to west <a href="/w/index.php?title=Metalrax&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Metalrax (page does not exist)">Metalrax</a>, headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Alvechurch" title="Alvechurch">Alvechurch</a> near the M42, make (via subsidiaries) most of the <a href="/wiki/Cookware_and_bakeware" title="Cookware and bakeware">bakeware</a> sold in the UK.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lea_%26_Perrins_worcestershire_sauce_150ml.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Lea_%26_Perrins_worcestershire_sauce_150ml.jpg/220px-Lea_%26_Perrins_worcestershire_sauce_150ml.jpg" width="220" height="294" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Lea_%26_Perrins_worcestershire_sauce_150ml.jpg/330px-Lea_%26_Perrins_worcestershire_sauce_150ml.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Lea_%26_Perrins_worcestershire_sauce_150ml.jpg/440px-Lea_%26_Perrins_worcestershire_sauce_150ml.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2030" data-file-height="2714" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lea_%26_Perrins_worcestershire_sauce_150ml.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The factory opened in 1897; the recipe for <a href="/wiki/Worcestershire_sauce" title="Worcestershire sauce">Worcestershire sauce</a> came from <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Sandys,_3rd_Baron_Sandys" title="Marcus Sandys, 3rd Baron Sandys">Lord Sandys</a>, and was only discovered accidentally when initially discarded and left to mature for months</div></div></div>\n<p>Roger Dyson Group manufactures <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_recovery" title="Vehicle recovery">auto-recovery</a> vehicles off the A442 in north Droitwich, near <a href="/wiki/Vax_(vacuum)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vax (vacuum)">Vax</a> and <a href="/wiki/Koito_Industries" class="mw-redirect" title="Koito Industries">Koito Europe</a> (car <a href="/wiki/Headlamp" title="Headlamp">headlamps</a>). South of Bromsgrove, on the B4091 at <a href="/wiki/Stoke_Prior,_Worcestershire" title="Stoke Prior, Worcestershire">Stoke Prior</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=L.G._Harris_%26_Co&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="L.G. Harris &amp; Co (page does not exist)">L.G. Harris &amp; Co</a> make <a href="/wiki/Paintbrush" title="Paintbrush">paintbrushes</a>. <a href="/wiki/Lea_%26_Perrins" title="Lea &amp; Perrins">Lea &amp; Perrins</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Worcester" title="Worcester">Worcester</a>. <a href="/wiki/Joy_Mining_Machinery" class="mw-redirect" title="Joy Mining Machinery">Joy Mining Machinery</a> are on the A44 in the west of Worcester. <a href="/wiki/Worcester,_Bosch_Group" title="Worcester, Bosch Group">Worcester, Bosch Group</a> make 1,200 boilers a day. <a href="/wiki/Yamazaki_Mazak_Corporation" title="Yamazaki Mazak Corporation">Mazak</a> UK have the parent company\'s European manufacturing facility (for <a href="/wiki/Numerical_control" title="Numerical control">CNC</a> machine tools) on the B4639 in the north of Worcester, next to the <a href="/wiki/Worcester_and_Birmingham_Canal" title="Worcester and Birmingham Canal">Worcester and Birmingham Canal</a>; nearby on the Blackpole Ind Est, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Froude_Hofmann&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Froude Hofmann (page does not exist)">Froude Hofmann</a> have their world headquarters, who make <a href="/wiki/Dynamometer" title="Dynamometer">dynamometers</a>, originated from <a href="/wiki/William_Froude" title="William Froude">William Froude</a> (former <a href="/wiki/Heenan_%26_Froude" title="Heenan &amp; Froude">Heenan &amp; Froude</a>). \n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sealine" title="Sealine">Sealine</a> make boats at the <a href="/wiki/A442_road" title="A442 road">A442</a>/A451 roundabout in Kidderminster, owned by <a href="/wiki/Brunswick_Boat_Group" title="Brunswick Boat Group">Brunswick Boat Group</a>. Also in Kidderminster of the A451, Stourport Road are <a href="/wiki/Brintons" title="Brintons">Brintons</a> Carpets and Beakbane. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Roxel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Roxel (page does not exist)">Roxel</a> UK (equally owned by <a href="/wiki/Safran" title="Safran">Safran</a> and <a href="/wiki/MBDA" title="MBDA">MBDA</a>), develops <a href="/wiki/Solid-fuel_rocket" class="mw-redirect" title="Solid-fuel rocket">solid-fuel rockets</a> for missiles at the A449/A442 junction south of Kidderminster and in <a href="/wiki/Hartlebury" title="Hartlebury">Hartlebury</a>, on the former site of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Ordnance_Rocket_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Royal Ordnance Rocket Motors (page does not exist)">Royal Ordnance Rocket Motors</a>. The <a href="/wiki/West_Midland_Safari_Park" title="West Midland Safari Park">West Midland Safari Park</a> is off the <a href="/wiki/A456_road" title="A456 road">A456</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bewdley" title="Bewdley">Bewdley</a>, west of Kidderminster. <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Technical_Ceramics" title="Morgan Technical Ceramics">Morgan Technical Ceramics</a> is headquartered on the B4195 at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lickhill&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lickhill (page does not exist)">Lickhill</a> in <a href="/wiki/Stourport-on-Severn" title="Stourport-on-Severn">Stourport-on-Severn</a>, south of Kidderminster; at the B4193/A4025 roundabout, <a href="/w/index.php?title=XTA_Electronics&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="XTA Electronics (page does not exist)">XTA Electronics</a> make audio amplifiers. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Egbert_H._Taylor&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Egbert H. Taylor (page does not exist)">Egbert H. Taylor</a> off the A442 in <a href="/wiki/Elmley_Lovett" title="Elmley Lovett">Elmley Lovett</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Hartlebury" title="Hartlebury">Hartlebury</a> is the world\'s leading manufacturer of metal bins. Leigh Sinton was the home of Biffa Waste Services\' Worcester depot until the closure in July 2013.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Qinetiq,_Malvern_-_geograph.org.uk_-_728922.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Qinetiq%2C_Malvern_-_geograph.org.uk_-_728922.jpg/220px-Qinetiq%2C_Malvern_-_geograph.org.uk_-_728922.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Qinetiq%2C_Malvern_-_geograph.org.uk_-_728922.jpg/330px-Qinetiq%2C_Malvern_-_geograph.org.uk_-_728922.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Qinetiq%2C_Malvern_-_geograph.org.uk_-_728922.jpg/440px-Qinetiq%2C_Malvern_-_geograph.org.uk_-_728922.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Qinetiq,_Malvern_-_geograph.org.uk_-_728922.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Qinetiq at the <a href="/wiki/Malvern_Hills_Science_Park" title="Malvern Hills Science Park">Malvern Hills Science Park</a>, or Malvern Technology Centre; the integrated circuit was invented here in 1952</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Liquid_crystal_display" class="mw-redirect" title="Liquid crystal display">Liquid crystal displays</a> were developed in 1972 in conjunction with the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Radar_Establishment" title="Royal Radar Establishment">Royal Radar Establishment</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Dummer" title="Geoffrey Dummer">Geoffrey Dummer</a> invented the idea of the <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">integrated circuit</a> in 1952. It was based in <a href="/wiki/Malvern,_Worcestershire" title="Malvern, Worcestershire">Malvern</a>, and became the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Signals_and_Radar_Establishment" title="Royal Signals and Radar Establishment">Royal Signals and Radar Establishment</a>, which developed <a href="/wiki/Thermography" title="Thermography">thermal imaging</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pyroelectricity" title="Pyroelectricity">pyroelectric</a> <a href="/wiki/Infrared_detector" title="Infrared detector">infrared detectors</a>, and is now a large site owned by <a href="/wiki/QinetiQ" class="mw-redirect" title="QinetiQ">QinetiQ</a>. <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Motor_Company" title="Morgan Motor Company">Morgan Motor Company</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Malvern_Link" title="Malvern Link">Malvern Link</a>; nearby is <a href="/wiki/Desire_Petroleum" title="Desire Petroleum">Desire Petroleum</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Commsoft_RMS&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Commsoft RMS (page does not exist)">Commsoft RMS</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Evesham" title="Evesham">Evesham</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Allen_Gears&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Allen Gears (page does not exist)">Allen Gears</a> supply industrial-sized gears off the A4104 in <a href="/wiki/Pershore" title="Pershore">Pershore</a>. For many years <a href="/wiki/Group_4_(company)" title="Group 4 (company)">Group 4 Security</a>, which was the largest security company in Europe, had its headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Broadway,_Worcestershire" title="Broadway, Worcestershire">Broadway</a> off the A44, on the edge of the <a href="/wiki/Cotswolds" title="Cotswolds">Cotswolds</a>; <a href="/wiki/G4S" title="G4S">G4S</a> Integrated Services now has its HQ there.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Midlands_(region)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KEASTON_Main.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/KEASTON_Main.jpg/220px-KEASTON_Main.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/KEASTON_Main.jpg/330px-KEASTON_Main.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/KEASTON_Main.jpg/440px-KEASTON_Main.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KEASTON_Main.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/King_Edward_VI_Aston_School" title="King Edward VI Aston School">King Edward VI Aston School</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ShrewsburySixthFormCollege.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/14/ShrewsburySixthFormCollege.JPG/220px-ShrewsburySixthFormCollege.JPG" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/14/ShrewsburySixthFormCollege.JPG/330px-ShrewsburySixthFormCollege.JPG 1.5x, class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ShrewsburySixthFormCollege.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Shrewsbury_Sixth_Form_College" title="Shrewsbury Sixth Form College">Shrewsbury Sixth Form College</a></div></div></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(January 2017)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary_education">Secondary education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Midlands_(region)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Secondary education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Selective schools are in low numbers as follows: Birmingham (8), Walsall (2), Wolverhampton (1), Warwickshire (6), Stoke-on-Trent (1), and Telford and Wrekin (2). The highest proportion per head therefore is Warwickshire (its population is between 550,000 and 600,000 people). The other counties and metropolitan boroughs have none, their public education systems are comprehensive in intake. The grammar and independent schools tend to produce pass-rate examination results among the top twenty ranked regionally. Many pupils compete for entrance examinations to attend such long-established <a href="/wiki/Grammar_schools_in_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammar schools in England">Grammar Schools</a> and most have significant parent sponsorship. In 2016 two of the top ten such schools nationally were in Warwickshire, where in the <a href="/wiki/CV_postcode_area" title="CV postcode area">CV37 postal district</a> prices were 34% higher than the county as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The top 20 schools at A-level rarely change from year to year; slightly lower in the table pass-rate boosts and top grades regularly occur among the schools receiving industrial funding, with similar frequency to London, the North East, and the North West, particularly in <a href="/wiki/Free_school_(England)" title="Free school (England)">schools</a> and <a href="/wiki/Academy_(English_school)" title="Academy (English school)">academies</a> which have some of the most advanced facilities.\n</p><p>Around 275,000 secondary schools are in the region, the greatest number after the <a href="/wiki/South_East_England" title="South East England">South East</a>, Greater London and <a href="/wiki/North_West_England" title="North West England">North West</a>. \n</p><p>At <a href="/wiki/GCSE" class="mw-redirect" title="GCSE">GCSE</a> based on&#160;% of entrants\' pass rates, the best performing local government area in 2010 was Solihull, closely followed by Warwickshire and Shropshire. Dudley, Herefordshire, Telford and Wrekin, Birmingham and Staffordshire (in descending order) are above the English average, at which rate, is approximately Worcestershire. The area consistently having fewest passes is Sandwell, followed by Stoke-on-Trent. Struggling pupils in Wolverhampton and Walsall also attain fewer passes than the English average in most GCSE years, sometimes by a very narrow margin. For metropolitan boroughs, Solihull then Dudley perform best. Dudley is the best metropolitan borough at A-level passes and has a consistent post-2000 history of being better than Solihull.\n</p><p>At A-level in 2010, the consistently best performing area was Herefordshire where most A-level candidates attend Hereford <a href="/wiki/Sixth_form_college" title="Sixth form college">sixth form college</a>. Dudley is also above the English average; the other metropolitan boroughs have low-to-average A-level pass or high mark proportions. Shropshire is at the English average.\n</p><p>Regionally in persistent <a href="/wiki/Truancy" title="Truancy">truancy</a> at secondary school, Sandwell had the highest rate at 6.9%; <a href="/wiki/Bromsgrove_(district)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bromsgrove (district)">Bromsgrove</a> had the lowest at 2.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tertiary_education">Tertiary education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Midlands_(region)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Tertiary education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There are thirty-seven FE colleges (FECs).<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> There are six LSCs for the area (which fund FECs), and the <a href="/wiki/Learning_and_Skills_Council" title="Learning and Skills Council">Learning and Skills Council</a> head office is based in <a href="/wiki/Coventry" title="Coventry">Coventry</a>. The five largest FE colleges in the region \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Bournville_College" title="Bournville College">Bournville College</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Warwickshire_and_Hinckley_College" title="North Warwickshire and Hinckley College">North Warwickshire and Hinckley College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solihull_College" title="Solihull College">Solihull College</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_%26_City_College_Birmingham" class="mw-redirect" title="South &amp; City College Birmingham">South &amp; City College Birmingham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stoke-on-Trent_College" title="Stoke-on-Trent College">Stoke-on-Trent College</a> \xe2\x80\x93 each have more than 25,000 students.\n</p><p>School children in Shropshire and Solihull are most likely to attend university, followed by Herefordshire, Worcestershire and Warwickshire.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="School_league_tables">School league tables</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Midlands_(region)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: School league tables">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Below is a list of the top thirty state schools in the West Midlands by 2010 A level results:\n</p>\n<ul><li>1. <a href="/w/index.php?title=King_Edward_VI_Camp_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="King Edward VI Camp Hill (page does not exist)">King Edward VI Camp Hill</a> School for Girls, Kings Heath (1212)</li>\n<li>2. <a href="/wiki/Sutton_Coldfield_Grammar_School_for_Girls" title="Sutton Coldfield Grammar School for Girls">Sutton Coldfield Grammar School for Girls</a></li>\n<li>3. <a href="/wiki/King_Edward_VI_Five_Ways" class="mw-redirect" title="King Edward VI Five Ways">King Edward VI Five Ways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bartley_Green" title="Bartley Green">Bartley School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Much_Wenlock" title="Much Wenlock">Much Wenlock</a> (880)</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Universities">Universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Birmingham_-_Aston_Webb.jpg" <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Birmingham_-_Aston_Webb.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>University of Birmingham</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Medical_teaching_centre_WU_4g07.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" Worcester</a>\n</td>\n<td>10,745\n</td>\n<td>97\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Keele_University" title="Keele University">Keele University</a>\n</td>\n<td>10,600\n</td>\n<td>46\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Harper_Adams_University" title="Harper Adams University">Harper Adams University</a>\n</td>\n<td>5,410\n</td>\n<td>46\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/University_College_Birmingham" title="University College Birmingham">University College Birmingham</a>\n</td>\n<td>4,935\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Newman_University,_Birmingham" title="Newman University, Birmingham">Newman University</a>\n</td>\n<td>2,830\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The University of Birmingham is the main university in the region<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> and has the most funding. It has a large research grant, as does the University of Warwick, which is the next largest in terms of funding. Birmingham and Warwick are members of the <a href="/wiki/Russell_Group" title="Russell Group">Russell Group</a> of public research universities. Keele and Aston have a moderate research grant, but none of the other universities do. Keele, although having the largest campus in the UK (by area), is one of the smallest universities in the region. There are medical schools are at <a href="/wiki/Warwick_Medical_School" title="Warwick Medical School">Warwick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keele_University_Medical_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Keele University Medical School">Keele</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Birmingham_Medical_School" title="University of Birmingham Medical School">Birmingham</a>. Birmingham and Warwick receive more than twice as much total income than any other university in the region \xe2\x80\x93 around \xc2\xa3400&#160;million each.\n</p><p>For students in the region, around 45% are from the region, and 35% from other regions. The other region with the most native students in the region is <a href="/wiki/South_East_England" title="South East England">South East England</a> (good access via the <a href="/wiki/M40_motorway" title="M40 motorway">M40</a> and the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a>), but there is a good mix of students from other regions, except the North East (especially) and Yorkshire.\n</p><p>Students native to the West Midlands are most likely to study in the region (40%), then the <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands" title="East Midlands">East Midlands</a> (12%), the <a href="/wiki/North_West_England" title="North West England">North West</a> (11%), and then Yorkshire (9%). Very few go to the <a href="/wiki/East_of_England" title="East of England">East of England</a> or the <a href="/wiki/North_East_England" title="North East England">North East</a>. The region has a net export of university students to other regions.\n</p><p>Once graduated, almost 60% of graduates stay in the region, with 10% going to London, 7% to the South-East, and around 5% to the East Midlands. Very few go to Yorkshire, the North-East, or even (neighbouring) Wales.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Midlands_(region)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Birmingham" title="Media in Birmingham">Media in Birmingham</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Midlands_(region)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ITV_Central_TV_studios_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1150068.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/ITV_Central_TV_studios_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1150068.jpg/220px-ITV_Central_TV_studios_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1150068.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/ITV_Central_TV_studios_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1150068.jpg/330px-ITV_Central_TV_studios_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1150068.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/ITV_Central_TV_studios_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1150068.jpg/440px-ITV_Central_TV_studios_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1150068.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ITV_Central_TV_studios_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1150068.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>ITV Central <a href="/wiki/Gas_Street_Studios" title="Gas Street Studios">Gas Street Studios</a> in Birmingham</div></div></div>\n<p>The West Midlands region of the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> is based at the <a href="/wiki/Mailbox_Birmingham" title="Mailbox Birmingham">Mailbox</a> in Birmingham. From there, the regional programme <a href="/wiki/Midlands_Today" title="Midlands Today">Midlands Today</a> is produced. <a href="/wiki/Central_Independent_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Independent Television">ITV Central</a> broadcasts from Birmingham, off <a href="/wiki/Broad_Street,_Birmingham" title="Broad Street, Birmingham">Broad Street</a> on <a href="/wiki/Gas_Street_Basin" title="Gas Street Basin">Gas Street</a> next to the <a href="/wiki/Worcester_and_Birmingham_Canal" title="Worcester and Birmingham Canal">Worcester and Birmingham Canal</a>, with its <a href="/wiki/ITV_News_Central" title="ITV News Central">ITV News Central</a> regional programme.\n</p><p>Some northern parts of the region, including <a href="/wiki/Biddulph" title="Biddulph">Biddulph</a>, receive <a href="/wiki/BBC_North_West_Tonight" title="BBC North West Tonight">BBC North West Tonight</a> and <a href="/wiki/Granada_Reports" title="Granada Reports">Granada Reports</a> both of which are based at <a href="/wiki/Media_City_UK" class="mw-redirect" title="Media City UK">Media City UK</a> in <a href="/wiki/City_of_Salford" title="City of Salford">Salford</a> and are broadcast from the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Hill_transmitting_station" title="Winter Hill transmitting station">Winter Hill</a> transmitter.\n</p><p>The BBC has its engineering training centre at <a href="/wiki/Wood_Norton,_Worcestershire" title="Wood Norton, Worcestershire">Wood Norton, Worcestershire</a>, off the A44 north of Evesham in Norton and Lenchwick. <a href="/wiki/BBC_English_Regions" title="BBC English Regions">BBC English Regions</a> is based at Birmingham.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Midlands_(region)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Shropshire" title="BBC Radio Shropshire">BBC Radio Shropshire</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_radio">Commercial radio</span><span include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Berrow%27s_Worcester_Journal" title="Berrow&#39;s Worcester Journal">Berrow\'s Worcester Journal</a></i></li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Mail" href="/wiki/Worcester_News" title="Worcester News">Worcester News</a></i></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Magazines">Magazines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Midlands_(region)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Magazines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>William Gibbons of Wolverhampton prints <i><a href="/wiki/New_Scientist" title="New Scientist">New Scientist</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lady_(magazine)" title="The Lady (magazine)">The Lady</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Farmers_Weekly" title="Farmers Weekly">Farmers Weekly</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/BBC_Focus" title="BBC Focus">BBC Focus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Psychologies" title="Psychologies">Psychologies</a></i>, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_Revealed&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="History Revealed (page does not exist)">History Revealed</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Classic_Rock_(magazine)" title="Classic Rock (magazine)">Classic Rock</a></i>, and <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tractors_%26_Machinery&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tractors &amp; Machinery (page does not exist)">Tractors &amp; Machinery</a></i>.\n</p><p>The Polestar Varnicoat works on the A44 in <a href="/wiki/Pinvin" title="Pinvin">Pinvin</a>, north of Pershore, for many years<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2016)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> printed <i><a href="/wiki/Woman%27s_Own" title="Woman&#39;s Own">Woman\'s Own</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Heat_(magazine)" title="Heat (magazine)">Heat</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pick_Me_Up_(magazine)" title="Pick Me Up (magazine)">Pick Me Up</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Chat_(magazine)" title="Chat (magazine)">Chat</a></i>, and <i>That\'s Life</i>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Online">Online</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Midlands_(region)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Online">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">Channel 4</a>\'s 4Talent network has a hub in the West Midlands dealing with rising media talent from the region.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Midlands_(region)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Birmingham" title="Sport in Birmingham">Sport in Birmingham</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Georges_Park_Aerial_May_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/St_Georges_Park_Aerial_May_2012.jpg/220px-St_Georges_Park_Aerial_May_2012.jpg" width="220" height="329" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/St_Georges_Park_Aerial_May_2012.jpg/330px-St_Georges_Park_Aerial_May_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/St_Georges_Park_Aerial_May_2012.jpg/440px-St_Georges_Park_Aerial_May_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3872" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Georges_Park_Aerial_May_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>St George\'s Park is the training ground of the <a href="/wiki/England_National_Football_Team" class="mw-redirect" title="England National Football Team">England National Football Team</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Sports_Centre" title="National Sports Centre">National Sports Centre</a> at <a href="/wiki/Lilleshall_Hall" title="Lilleshall Hall">Lilleshall Hall</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Sheriffhales" title="Sheriffhales">Sheriffhales</a>, Shropshire, north-east of Telford; it was largely established by the <a href="/wiki/Sport_and_Recreation_Alliance" title="Sport and Recreation Alliance">Central Council of Physical Recreation</a> in 1949 as a National Recreation Centre; the south of England had theirs at <a href="/wiki/Bisham_Abbey" title="Bisham Abbey">Bisham Abbey</a> on the Thames. <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Park_National_Football_Centre" title="St George&#39;s Park National Football Centre">St George\'s Park National Football Centre</a> is at <a href="/wiki/Tatenhill" title="Tatenhill">Tatenhill</a> near <a href="/w/index.php?title=Byrkley_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Byrkley Park (page does not exist)">Byrkley Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Needwood_Forest" title="Needwood Forest">Needwood Forest</a>, near former the <a href="/wiki/RAF_Tatenhill" title="RAF Tatenhill">RAF Tatenhill</a> off the <a href="/wiki/A515_road" title="A515 road">A515</a>, four miles west of Burton upon Trent.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Tough_Guy_Competition" title="Tough Guy Competition">Tough Guy Competition</a>, now a widespread sport competition in the USA, began in 1987 on a farm at <a href="/wiki/Perton" title="Perton">Perton</a> in Staffordshire. The main British athletics championships are held in Birmingham in late June. The <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">Olympic Movement</a> started at <a href="/wiki/Much_Wenlock" title="Much Wenlock">Much Wenlock</a>, and also to the east of region, where <a href="/wiki/Pierre_de_Coubertin" title="Pierre de Coubertin">Baron de Coubertin</a> formulated his ideas for sport and the Olympics at <a href="/wiki/Rugby_School" title="Rugby School">Rugby School</a> in 1883, with the headmaster <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Arnold" title="Thomas Arnold">Thomas Arnold</a>, whose son would be the famous poet <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Arnold" title="Matthew Arnold">Matthew Arnold</a> and whose great-grandson would be <a href="/wiki/Aldous_Huxley" title="Aldous Huxley">Aldous Huxley</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a Ground\n</td>\n<td>5,000\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby">Rugby</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Midlands_(region)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Rugby">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, the region is home to professional <a href="/wiki/English_Premiership_(rugby_union)" class="mw-redirect" title="English Premiership (rugby union)">Premiership</a> teams <a href="/wiki/Wasps_RFC" title="Wasps RFC">Wasps RFC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Worcester_Warriors" title="Worcester Warriors">Worcester Warriors</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coventry_Bears" title="Coventry Bears">Coventry Bears</a> play in the third tier <a href="/wiki/League_1_(rugby_league)" title="League 1 (rugby league)">League 1</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tennis">Tennis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Midlands_(region)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Tennis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_tennis" title="History of tennis">History of tennis</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tennis_Match,_Family_Circle_Cup_2008.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Tennis_Match%2C_Family_Circle_Cup_2008.JPG/220px-Tennis_Match%2C_Family_Circle_Cup_2008.JPG" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Tennis_Match%2C_Family_Circle_Cup_2008.JPG/330px-Tennis_Match%2C_Family_Circle_Cup_2008.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Tennis_Match%2C_Family_Circle_Cup_2008.JPG/440px-Tennis_Match%2C_Family_Circle_Cup_2008.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2641" data-file-height="3976" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tennis_Match,_Family_Circle_Cup_2008.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tennis was invented in Edgbaston, Birmingham</div></div></div>\n<p>Britain\'s first tennis club was founded in 1872 in <a href="/wiki/Royal_Leamington_Spa" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Leamington Spa">Leamington Spa</a>. The modern rules of lawn tennis were developed in 1874 by Leamington Tennis Club. Tennis was pioneered in Edgbaston in 1859, and <a href="/wiki/Edgbaston_Archery_and_Lawn_Tennis_Society" title="Edgbaston Archery and Lawn Tennis Society">Edgbaston Archery and Lawn Tennis Society</a> also claims to be the oldest tennis club in the world, where tennis was invented by Major <a href="/wiki/Harry_Gem" title="Harry Gem">Harry Gem</a> and the Spaniard <a href="/wiki/Augurio_Perera" title="Augurio Perera">Augurio Perera</a>.\n</p><p>A famous 1970s <a href="/wiki/Tennis_Girl" title="Tennis Girl">Tennis Girl</a> picture was taken on 12 September 1976 by Oldbury\'s <a href="/wiki/Martin_Elliott" title="Martin Elliott">Martin Elliott</a> at the tennis courts of Birmingham University, featuring 18-year-old Fiona Butler, now of <a href="/wiki/Stourport-on-Severn" title="Stourport-on-Severn">Stourport-on-Severn</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Motor_sport">Motor sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Midlands_(region)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Motor sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Team_Dynamics" title="Team Dynamics">Team Dynamics</a> at <a href="/wiki/Pershore" title="Pershore">Pershore</a>, has won the <a href="/wiki/British_Touring_Car_Championship" title="British Touring Car Championship">British Touring Car Championship</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Midlands_(region)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 2001 part of the White Other category. New category created for the 2011 census</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-19">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 2001 part of the \'Other\' category.
